< text>
Attending our son's PhD graduation we found the The Pavilion to be an excellent faculty for such functions.  Temperature inside was very comfortable.  No matter where one was sitting, you had excellent views of the festivities.  The audio system was understandable and the video screen gave a good close up of each graduate receiving their degree<//text>

< review>
Okay selection, but terrible price management and not the best customer service. Items are priced at a flat rate (i.e. all dresses are $9.00). I brought a Forever 21 dress to the counter and let the lady working know that this dress would have cost $12.00 in-store and they have some dresses that retailed less than what they sell them for. This is an illegal retail practice (I manage a consignment and thrift store). I let the worker know, and she told me to speak with management. They also have some designer items that could be sold for a lot higher prices, had they done their research. Store worker told me that they do not research original retail prices, just randomized numbers they chose. This is a MAJOR flaw in the thrift industry, don't get fooled! But look for the designer items that they haven't validated, and of course, look out for fake merchandise.<//review>

< text>
Nice and clean place. They put up some nice paintings/posters which adds to the classy factor. If you're looking for furniture, jewelry, or clothes this is probably your place. Overall it doesn't have much floor space and there's just one small shelf for electronics which was basically void. I asked if I could see more and got the, "what's on the floor only" response which I understand but the guy in front of me just purchased something from the back (why I even bothered asking) so I don't appreciate the hypocrisy. They also make up prices at checkout which I imagine could be very frustrating, and another reason why not letting me see more doesn't make sense, it's not like they can't show you because it hasn't been valued yet.< /text>

<rate>3< /rate><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Time>1553742330507<//Time>< Text>
The Rainbow Crepe Cake was great! Lots of layers to it and a responsible amount of cream between each layer. Hard to keep it from sliding without a knife to cut it, so be advised.

The mini macaroons looked good, but I didn't order any.

Unfortunately, I asked for a Taro Latte and the girl at the register did not ask if I wanted it to be hot or iced. I assumed it would be hot because it's a latte. She gave me an * Iced * Taro Latte back. This ruined my experience. It was the only thing I came in for.

Later, I talked with the young man there (the girl went to the back room). He was very generous about it and offered me the hot item to make up for it. I declined, because I didn't want 2 lattes, but it was a nice gesture.

He seemed overly respectful, even before my complaint, which I enjoyed.

Otherwise, this place seems nice but I would like to see it look cozier. The interior could be more comfy.<//Text>

I figured out the problem:  Galpin Subaru is actually now closed.  I think it's now a Porsche dealer (See attached screenshot) so the mechanics, who probably got wind of this a while ago stopped "bothering" to change the oil and any other "non-essential" service items which wouldn't immediately be missed.

I've been checking my Subaru Tribeca like clockwork and it never seems to burn any oil.  For it to get 5.75 qts. empty they must have last checked\changed the oil in about 2014.   Thanks Subaru for keeping an eye on these dealerships.

........................

Wow, when I wrote this original review (below) two years ago seems to be about the same time these guys actually changed or checked the oil in our Subaru Tribeca.  I have had four visits to this dealer this year (2018) for stuff like a leaking fuel cap, idler belt, full service etc., and it would seem that nobody actually checks the oil during the multi-point inspection.  It's been in the shop a LOT.  Did nobody think to check the oil?  Yeah, yeah, I know it's the customer's obligation to (according to Subaru), check it every other fill-up) but how many people do YOU know who checks their car's oil regularly any more? And at every other gas fill-up?? To save time my suspicion is that they (the mechanics) just tick off the box on the paperwork - after all, who's gonna know?  Either that or it used 5.5 quarts of oil in one month.  Burning a lot, leaking?  -- There are NO drip spots in my garage and no smokey pipes.  My advice is to check your own oil and check it while still at the dealer to make sure they actually did do something.  How did I find out?  I couldn't figure out what was wrong with the car so, on a road trip I visited Firestone (who were great).  The oil level was so low the guys at Firestone were amazed it hadn't seized up.  Beware and be forewarned.  I used to check the oil regularly but over the years, because it never seemed to need any, lost the habit.  So it seems did the @Subaru mechanics at Galpin Subaru.

< review>
On if the best pleasures in life is sitting and having a meal and everyone is reaching for the food without complaining. This is very rare in my family. Almost at every restaurant someone is unhappy with the food choice. Nothere. They have shabushabu which is soup based and ikiniku which is grilled based.  You cook on the table and the staff there teaches you what to do. It was great and highly recommend. I suggest the spicy soup based which is not really spicy. Do ask for soup bowls. All the beef they has was good quality and tasty. Don't be intimidated go in and just ask them to explain or recommend. Good Luck<//review>

<user_name>John Wie< /user_name><Date>1433972109658<//Date>< Rating>
4</Rating>
< Review>
If you've been to one Shin-Sen-Gumi, you kinda know how the system works and this one isn't different in terms of quality and taste.  However, if you haven't been, this Shin-Sen-Gumi is focused on shabu-shabu for an affordable price and always stellar service.  Waits can vary (on a Wednesday night, we waited for less than 10 minutes) and went mainly for the late night happy hour (which happens from Mon. - Thurs. - 8-11PM).  You pay about $18 for all-you-can eat beef shabu shabu.  It won't be the best quality meat and you'll have to pay more for extras but it's a solid meal and they have a ton of other options available from side dishes to beer/sake.  Parking is plentiful with a private lot.< /Review>

This review is for the Dollar Tree on Serramonte Blvd. I like this store. Most of the staff is very pleasant and generally helpful. Parking is usually available but carts can be hard to come by if they're busy.  If you see one in the lot, you would be wise to bring it with you into the store. The store is generally clean, though the bathroom could be cleaner. My pet peeve is that there's always too much stuff in the aisles. They block access to shelves and products, and make it difficult to get your cart down the aisle. It can be hard to get out of the lot because of the constant traffic on Serramonte.<//Text>
